    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="de7cee3baa244839bc6e3580152f52ed">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: '35955826-89ea-42f5-a47b-e5e29b0e2bd4'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en" style="">
         <h2 id="d37607442" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>Layered oxides are considered to be potential cathodes for sodium-ion batteries based on high theoretical capacity and ease of synthesis. However, the complex phase transition caused by interlayer sliding in layered oxides leads to poor cycling stability, which will hinder their further application. Here, we designed a newly O3-type layered cathode NaNi<sub>0.3</sub>Co<sub>0.2</sub>Cu<sub>0.1</sub>Mn<sub>0.2</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> based on high-entropy to achieve highly reversible phase transition behavior. It reveals 132 mAh g<sup>竏1</sup> at 0.2 C within 2窶4&nbsp;V increasing the energy density to 408窶姥h窶洩g<sup>竏1</sup> and it shows an outstanding rate capability of 90 mAh g<sup>竏1</sup> at 80 C (84.90% capacity retention after 1,500窶営ycles at 80 C). In-situ XRD shows that reasonable design of high-entropy components in layered material can achieve the purpose of delaying the occurrence of phase transition and DFT calculations show that the introduction of Co in transition metal layers can effectively improve the rate performance of the material. This work is of great significance in guiding the design and synthesis of highly stable layered cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="apj3116-sec-0001">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="apj3116-sec-0001-title">1 INTRODUCTION</h2>
         
         <p>Considering sodium resources are plentiful and extensively dispersed across the Earth's crust, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are currently being explored as potential alternatives for large-scale energy storage.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0001_R_d37607434e438" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Chem Soc Rev">1</a></sup></span> Generally, the selection of suitable cathode materials is crucial to the cycle stability and rate performance of batteries.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0002_R_d37607434e441" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - ACS Omega">2</a>, <a href="#apj3116-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0003_R_d37607434e441" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Chem Rev">3</a></sup></span> Prussian blue compounds, organic compounds, polyanionic compounds, and layered oxides are some of the different kinds of cathode materials for SIBs. One of the most studied cathode materials for SIBs is layered oxides because of their high energy density and simple synthesis process.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0004_R_d37607434e444" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - J Energy Chem">4</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <p>A series of layered oxides have been studied in recent years: Ma et al prepared O3-NaNi<sub>1/3</sub> Fe<sub>1/3</sub> Mn<sub>1/3</sub> O<sub>2</sub> by Fe doping via coprecipitation method, which can provide 120 mAh g<sup>竏1</sup> capacity over a voltage range of 2窶4&nbsp;V, which is regarded as a forerunner of commercially available cathode materials.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0005_R_d37607434e460" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Small">5</a></sup></span> Subsequently Wang et al synthesized O3-NaNi<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.3</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> by doping Ti element on the basis of transition metals as Ni and Mn via solid state method.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0006_R_d37607434e471" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - J Power Sources">6</a></sup></span> In order to further reduce the material cost, Hu's team found that Cu<sup>2+</sup> can provide some charge compensation due to the possibility of being oxidized to Cu<sup>3+</sup> and prepare cathode materials with low Ni content, and proposed O3-NaCu<sub>1/9</sub>Ni<sub>2/9</sub>Fe<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and O3-Na<sub>0.9</sub>Cu<sub>0.22</sub>Fe<sub>0.30</sub>Mn<sub>0.48</sub>O<sub>2</sub> containing Cu as cathode materials for SIBs.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0007_R_d37607434e501" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Energy Storage Sci Tech">7</a>, <a href="#apj3116-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0008_R_d37607434e501" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv Mater">8</a></sup></span> But the O3-type structures generally undergo complex phase transitions process during the process of charge and discharge, which limits the material ability to cycle and its structural stability.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0009_R_d37607434e504" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - J Phys Chem C">9</a></sup></span> 窶廩igh-entropy strategy窶 has been studied widely recently in the layered oxide areas ascribed to effectively delaying the occurrence of phase transitions and optimizing the electrochemical performance.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0010_R_d37607434e507" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Angew Chem in Ed">10</a></sup></span> High-entropy oxide can be regarded as a single-phase oxide system composed of five or more different cations, which has certain requirements for its configuration entropy, which is greater than 1.5R (R general gas constant), and when the configurational entropy is within the interval of 1.0R窶円窶1.5R for medium-entropy materials, and the configurational entropy is less than 1.0R for low-entropy materials.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0011_R_d37607434e510" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Scr Mater">11</a>, <a href="#apj3116-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0012_R_d37607434e510" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - APL Mater">12</a></sup></span> Multicomponent transition metals in high entropy materials can reduce the negative effects of local interactions during de-sodiation, which greatly influences layered cathode material energy density improvement and excellent cycle stability.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0013_R_d37607434e513" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Energ Environ Sci">13</a>, <a href="#apj3116-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0014_R_d37607434e513" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Small Methods">14</a></sup></span> In addition, the entropic stability and the interactions occurring between different doping elements also endow the high-entropy materials with unique structural stability.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0015_R_d37607434e516" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Science">15</a></sup></span> Hu's team combined the 窶徂igh entropy窶 concept and successfully prepared O3-type layered cathode materials NaNi<sub>0.12</sub>Cu<sub>0.12</sub>Mg<sub>0.12</sub>Fe<sub>0.15</sub>Co<sub>0.15</sub>Mn<sub>0.1</sub>Ti<sub>0.1</sub>Sn<sub>0.1</sub>Sb<sub>0.04</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and NaNi<sub>0.25</sub>Mg<sub>0.05</sub> Cu<sub>0.1</sub>Fe<sub>0.2</sub>Mn<sub>0.2</sub>Ti<sub>0.1</sub>Sn<sub>0.1</sub>O<sub>2</sub> for SIBs.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0016_R_d37607434e559" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - J am Chem Soc">16</a></sup></span> Tian et al designed and prepared a new six-component high-entropy layered cathode O3-NaFe<sub>0.2</sub>Co<sub>0.2</sub>Ni<sub>0.2</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>Sn<sub>0.1</sub>Li<sub>0.1</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, at 0.1 C and 2 C, respectively, the reversible capacities of this cathode were 112.7 mAh g<sup>竏1</sup> and 80.8 mAh g<sup>竏1</sup>.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0017_R_d37607434e581" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - J Mater Chem a">17</a></sup></span> And that, the selection of transition metal elements is of significant importance for forming high-entropy layered cathodes with stable structure. For transition metals, where doping Ni<sup>2+</sup> and Co<sup>3+</sup> can provide charge compensation to increase the capacity; Zhou et al concluded that Ti<sup>4+</sup> doping improves the stability of the layered oxide material under high voltage pressure, which can be explained by the stability of lattice oxygens; Cu<sup>2+</sup> improves reversibility and kinetics; the abundance of Mn<sup>4+</sup> makes it possible to act as a certain structure-forming agent.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0018_R_d37607434e595" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - J Alloys Compd">18</a>-<a href="#apj3116-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0024_R_d37607434e595" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Energy Storage Mater">24</a></sup></span> The components in the transition metal oxides are reasonably designed by comparing the advantages of transition metal elements in various cathode materials, the differences in electrochemistry, and the compatibility of redox reactions.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0025_R_d37607434e598" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Small">25</a>-<a href="#apj3116-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0028_R_d37607434e598" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Chem Commun">28</a></sup></span> Therefore, we chose to prepare O3-type five-component high-entropy oxides NaNi<sub>0.3</sub>Co<sub>0.2</sub>Cu<sub>0.1</sub> Mn<sub>0.2</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub>(NCCMT)as the cathode materials for SIBs to achieve the high rate performance and long cycle life of the layered materials.</p>
         
         <p>High-entropy doping strategy is designed and new O3-NaNi<sub>0.3</sub>Co<sub>0.2</sub>Cu<sub>0.1</sub>Mn<sub>0.2</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (NCCMT) cathode materials are prepared by sol窶堵el method in this paper. It shows that the NCCMT cathode material has excellent rate performance: within the voltage range of 2窶4&nbsp;V at 80 C, the discharge specific capacity can reach 90 mAh g<sup>竏1</sup> and the capacity retention is 84.90% even after 1,500窶営ycles. The specific discharge capacity can reach 132 mAh g<sup>竏1</sup> at 0.2 C, and the capacity retention rate is still more than 80% after 200窶営ycles. By in-situ X-ray diffraction (XRD), NCCMT undergoes O3-P3-O3 phase reversible transformation during charging and discharging, which exhibits good crystal structure stability. Density functional theory (DFT) computational studies further demonstrated that Co-doping in high-entropy configurations reduces the energy barrier of Na<sup>+</sup>, thereby exhibiting excellent rate properties. Our study found that the high entropy construction not only effectively improves the rate performance of layered materials, but also delays the occurrence of phase transition and improves the cycle performance. This work offers distinctive ideas for designing high-entropy configurations to further improve the rate performance for SIBs.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="apj3116-sec-0002">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="apj3116-sec-0002-title">2 EXPERIMENTAL SECTION</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="apj3116-sec-0003">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="apj3116-sec-0003-title">2.1 Synthesis of cathode materials</h3>
            
            <p>The sol窶堵el method was used in this work to prepare O3-type NaNi<sub>0.3</sub>Co<sub>0.2</sub>Cu<sub>0.1</sub>Mn<sub>0.2</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub>(NCCMT). Firstly, the stoichiometric ratios of NaNO<sub>3</sub>, Ni (CH<sub>3</sub>COO)<sub>2</sub>ﾂｷ4H<sub>2</sub>O, Co (NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>2</sub>ﾂｷ6H<sub>2</sub>O, CuC<sub>4</sub>H<sub>6</sub>O<sub>4</sub>ﾂｷH<sub>2</sub>O and MnC<sub>4</sub>H<sub>6</sub>O<sub>4</sub>ﾂｷ4H<sub>2</sub>O are added to the beaker and mixed with anhydrous ethanol to form a uniform precursor solution. After stirring and heating at 80ﾂｰC in a water bath, citric acid was slowly added dropwise and continued to be heated and stirred, forming a homogeneous sol as the solvent continued to evaporate. Dried in a vacuum drying oven at 110ﾂｰC to form a dry gel, fully ground and placed in a muffle furnace at 400ﾂｰC for pre-sintering 6&nbsp;h, cooled and removed to add TiO<sub>2</sub> (MACKLIN, 99.9%) in an agate mortar and continued to be fully ground, placed in a ceramic crucible and sintered in a muffle furnace at 900ﾂｰC for 20窶栄. After the sample cooled to room temperature, it was transferred to a glove box filled with Ar gas for storage.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="apj3116-sec-0004">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="apj3116-sec-0004-title">2.2 Electrochemical measurement</h3>
            
            <p>N-methylpyrrolidone (NMP) is the solvent, polytetrafluoroethylene (PVDF) is the binder, and acetylene black is the conducting agent. The material NCCMT is utilized as the cathode active substance. Following mass-ratio of 7: 2:1 for the active substance, conductive agent, and binder, the solvent is added and well mixed to create the slurry. To create the cathode electrode sheet, the slurry is spread out over aluminum foil and dried in a vacuum drying oven for a minimum of 10&nbsp;h. The anode is made of metal Na, and the battery is put together in an Ar-filled glove box. The electrolyte is 1.0&nbsp;M NaClO4 in PC: EC: DMC窶=窶1:1:1 Vol% with 2% FEC. Based on specific testing requirements, the LandBT2001A battery test system was chosen for electrochemical testing with a voltage window of 2窶4&nbsp;V/2窶4.3&nbsp;V and a current density of 0.1 C, 0.5 C, 1 C, 5 C, 10 C, 20 C, 50 C, and 80 C.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="apj3116-sec-0005">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="apj3116-sec-0005-title">2.3 Materials characterization</h3>
            
            <p>The synthesis of single-phase layered oxide compounds becomes increasingly difficult as the diversity of precursor components grows. Fortunately, as Figure&nbsp;<a href="#apj3116-fig-0001">1a</a> illustrates, newly designed NCCMT cathode materials have been effectively synthesized using the method known as sol窶堵el. Each major diffraction peak was well matched to the pure highly crystalline O3 structure (space group: <i>R</i><sup><i>竏</i></sup><i>3&nbsp;m</i>).<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0029_R_d37607434e722" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Energy Storage Mater">29</a></sup></span> Further analysis of the refined lattice parameters of NCCMT is a窶=窶2.95&nbsp;ﾃ, b窶=窶2.95&nbsp;ﾃ, c窶=窶16.20&nbsp;ﾃ. Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> displays additional lattice characteristics in more detail. The elemental proportions of NCCMT were detected as indicated in Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> using inductively coupled plasma (ICP), the ratios of Ni, Co, Cu, Mn, and Ti are 0.3:0.204:0.097:0.199:0.243, which is basically consistent with the design ratios of target material of NCCMT.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="apj3116-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/681fde17-c401-4de1-8b19-489e46eede46/apj3116-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/681fde17-c401-4de1-8b19-489e46eede46/apj3116-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/32dbd3da-408d-44c8-9ece-05f8bfa539dd/apj3116-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/681fde17-c401-4de1-8b19-489e46eede46/apj3116-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">FIGURE 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=apj3116-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fapj.3116" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Features of the NCCMT cathode structure and morphology as prepared. (a) Rietveld refinement plot of NCCMT. The inset schematically shows the crystalline structure of NCCMT. (b) TEM and (c) enlarged HRTEM images of NCCMT. (d) SEM-EDS mapping of NCCMT material.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            
            <p>Images captured by transmission electron microscopy (TEM) Figure&nbsp;<a href="#apj3116-fig-0001">1</a>(b-c) displays obvious crystal lattice fringes of the material. The measured spacing of adjacent crystal fringes is 0.542窶穎m, which corresponds to the (003) plane of O3-type layered material. The measured spacing of adjacent crystal fringes is 0.542窶穎m, showing that the sodium ions and transition metal ions are arranged in a well-ordered arrangement within the material. With no obvious segregation phenomenon, the whole particle of NCCMT has different components of Na, Co, Ni, Ti, Cu, and O dispersed uniformly throughout, according to the mapping from the scanning electron microscope energy dispersive spectrometer (SEM-EDS) shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#apj3116-fig-0001">1d</a>. Additionally, Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> of the SEM-EDS data demonstrates that the measured concentrations of all the elements are in close proximity to the designed stoichiometry (Ni: Co: Cu: Mn: Ti窶=窶3:2:1:2:2), which is consistent with the ICP results.</p>
            </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="apj3116-sec-0006">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="apj3116-sec-0006-title">3 RESULTS AND DISCUSSION</h2>
         
         <p>An analysis of the electrochemical performance of the NCCMT cathode was performed to study the impact of high-entropy configuration of the cathode material. The capacity of the first cycle is 132 mAh g<sup>竏1</sup> at 0.2 C(1 C窶=窶100&nbsp;mA窶曳<sup>竏1</sup>) within 2窶4&nbsp;V, as displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#apj3116-fig-0002">2a</a>. And after 200窶営ycles, the capacity retention is 81.92% (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>). Furthermore, the specific energy density of discharging is as high as 408窶姥h窶洩g<sup>竏1</sup> within the voltage range of 2窶4&nbsp;V. The relevant cathodes were compared, and the corresponding data are presented in Table&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0024_R_d37607434e790" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Energy Storage Mater">24</a></sup></span> The charge窶電ischarge curves of NCCMT cathode material consist of a longer platform at around 2.75窶鰻 between 2 and 4&nbsp;V compared to the voltage window at 2窶4.3&nbsp;V. The slope region correlates to the solid-solution process, and the platforms at around 2.75窶鰻 typically reflect the phase transition reaction that takes place during the de-sodiation process of the O3-type layered material.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0030_R_d37607434e793" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - J Mater Chem a">30</a></sup></span> It can be seen that the change in phase between the O3 and P3 of the NCCMT cathode material is more obvious in high voltage, and the voltage hysteresis phenomenon increases to some extent. The specific discharge capacity is 135.6 mAh g<sup>竏1</sup> at 0.2 C for the first cycle between 2 and 4.3&nbsp;V. It can be seen that the voltage decay phenomenon is more significant within 2窶4.3&nbsp;V compared to that within 2窶4&nbsp;V.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="apj3116-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/d0247df2-a990-46a6-8702-24dd15cb43fb/apj3116-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/d0247df2-a990-46a6-8702-24dd15cb43fb/apj3116-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/90942850-c932-46dc-8255-d73a373160ff/apj3116-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/d0247df2-a990-46a6-8702-24dd15cb43fb/apj3116-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">FIGURE 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=apj3116-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fapj.3116" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">First charge/discharge curves for the NCCMT cathode at 2窶4&nbsp;V (a) and 2窶4.3&nbsp;V (b) at 0.2 C. (c) Rate capability of NCCMT cathode at various rates from 2 to 4&nbsp;V. (d) Cycling performance of NCCMT cathode at 80 C.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>Furthermore, the rate performance of the NCCMT cathode was evaluated between 2 and 4&nbsp;V at 0.1 C, 0.5 C, 1 C, 5 C, 10 C, 20 C, 40 C, 50 C, and 80 C, respectively, according to Figure&nbsp;<a href="#apj3116-fig-0002">2c</a>. A 90 mAh g<sup>竏1</sup> is the specific discharge capacity displayed even at the ultra-high rate of 80 C, suggesting the excellent rate performance of the NCCMT cathode. Upon reaching 0.1 C again for the current density, the material capacity was restored to the initial discharge-specific capacity, proving the exceptional reversibility of the NCCMT cathode material for sodium storage. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, the discharge platform gradually weakened and shifted downward as the current density increased, which indicates that the complex phase transition of the O3-phase high-entropy layered cathode material is suppressed, and thus superior diffusion rate of Na<sup>+</sup> was obtained. In addition, it also demonstrated a long-cycle life with a cycling retention of 84.9% after 1,500窶営ycles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#apj3116-fig-0002">2d</a>), which exceeded most of the reported layered cathode materials for SIBs.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0031_R_d37607434e835" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - J Energy Storage">31</a>-<a href="#apj3116-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0033_R_d37607434e835" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - J Taiwan Inst Chem E">33</a></sup></span> The excellent electrochemical properties also demonstrate the practicality of the material within 2窶4&nbsp;V.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0034_R_d37607434e838" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - ACS Appl Mater Interfaces">34</a></sup></span> The rate capability at a wide voltage range between 2 and 4.3&nbsp;V of NCCMT cathode material had been performed in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>. Deoxygenation of the material surface under high voltage may be the cause of lower first-cycle Coulombic efficiency.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0035_R_d37607434e844" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Nature Sustainability">35</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <p>Long-term cycling between 2 and 4&nbsp;V voltage range at high current densities of 20 C and 50 C are displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, there is basically no degradation in capacity at both 20 C and 50 C current density after 800窶営ycles. Moreover, the material electrochemical reactions during the charging and discharging process are reversible, as evidenced by the Coulombic efficiency, which is nearly 100%. In contrast, the cycling performance has also been tested between 2 and 4.3&nbsp;V as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>. The capacity retention has decayed to 61.72% after 800窶営ycles at 80 C. Therefore, the 2窶4&nbsp;V voltage range was selected to perform the further electrochemical test and corresponding mechanism study of phase transition within NCCMT cathode material.</p>
         
         <p>To reveal the phase transition mechanism in more detail and the structural evolution of the cathode electrode during de-insertion of-, the in-situ XRD patterns were collected during the first charging/discharging process in the voltage range of 2窶4&nbsp;V at 0.1 C (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#apj3116-fig-0003">3</a>). The initial phase transition is such that as charging proceeds, the (003) and (006) peaks gradually move toward lower angles while de-sodiation initially started, indicating the increase of the interlayer spacing. While the (101) and (012) peaks gradually moved toward higher angles, which represent the in-plane bond lengths along the ab-axis.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0036_R_d37607434e862" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Inorg Chem Front">36</a></sup></span> When the battery was charged, the P3 phase emerged at about 2.8&nbsp;V. This is because Na<sup>+</sup> de-intercalation increased the repulsive forces between the oxide layers, which led to the sliding of the TMO<sub>2</sub> layer.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0037_R_d37607434e869" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - J Energy Chem">37</a></sup></span> Around 3&nbsp;V, the O3 phase diffraction peak (104) vanished following a brief period of the P3 and O3 phases coexisting and the diffraction peak of the P3 phase continued to move to a higher angle and increased in intensity until charging up to 4&nbsp;V, demonstrating the presence of a P3 solid solution reaction.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0038_R_d37607434e873" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Ceram Int">38</a></sup></span> Upon charging to 4&nbsp;V, the interlayer spacing reveals the maximum value, while it remains the P3 phase crystal structure, suggesting that this segment corresponds to a change in the order of Na<sup>+</sup> vacancies.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0039_R_d37607434e878" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Nano Res">39</a>, <a href="#apj3116-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0040_R_d37607434e878" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Angew Chem Int Ed">40</a></sup></span> The phase transition process of the subsequent discharging is totally reversible to the charging process with P3-O3. However, it is worth noting that when discharged to 3&nbsp;V, the (003) peak is moved to the higher angles, and the intensity of (104) peak is enhanced, indicating that the material starts to transform into the O3 phase. While the characteristic peaks of the P3 phase disappear completely only when discharged to 2.75窶鰻 and it go back to the O3 phase when discharged to 2&nbsp;V, which suggests the structural stability of the NCCMT cathode material.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="apj3116-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/6d595d14-3803-4a42-a826-85e81dbdbb28/apj3116-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/6d595d14-3803-4a42-a826-85e81dbdbb28/apj3116-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/9b05b9dc-c98b-4be0-bbe9-7c437b409060/apj3116-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/6d595d14-3803-4a42-a826-85e81dbdbb28/apj3116-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">FIGURE 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=apj3116-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fapj.3116" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">The initial cycle of the NCCMT cathode at 0.1 C with 2窶4&nbsp;V is shown by the structural evolution contour plots of the in-situ XRD patterns. The right side shows the corresponding a-axis and c-axis lattice parameters calculated from the refined results.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>The specific changes in the refined parameters of NCCMT crystal structure over the initial charge/discharge cycle from 2&nbsp;V to 4&nbsp;V are summarized on the right side in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#apj3116-fig-0003">3</a>. It shows that the high-entropy strategy has lower structural shrinkage expansion. The design of complex components in high-entropy materials can inhibit the orderly arrangement of charges in the transition metal layer, and reasonable elemental substitution to reduce phase transitions, especially those in the high voltage region that can cause large volume changes, realize the use of sodium-ion layered oxides at higher capacities (as close as possible to the theoretical specific capacity).<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0041_R_d37607434e907" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Adv Energy Mater">41</a>-<a href="#apj3116-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0045_R_d37607434e907" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Carbon Neutralization">45</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <p>In order to clarify the reason for such excellent rate performance within NCCMT cathode material, DFT calculations based on NCMT (without Co doping) and NCCMT (with Co doping) were applied and the detailed results are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#apj3116-fig-0004">4</a>. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#apj3116-fig-0004">4a</a>, the migration barriers of Na<sup>+</sup> in NCMT and NCCMT were calculated to be 0.601窶影V and 0.502窶影V, respectively. Obviously, NCCMT cathode after Co doping with the high-entropy configuration requires lower energy for sodium ion migration, since the unpaired electron Mn<sup>3+</sup> exhibits a significant Jahn-Teller effect, distortion of the lattice structure and charge ordering was induced, thus Na<sup>+</sup> migration will be limited.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0046_R_d37607434e925" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - J Energy Chem">46</a></sup></span> And Co doping can effectively attenuate the distortion of the Jahn-Teller effect of Mn<sup>3+</sup>, and the crystal structure is more stable. Then the phase transition does not easily occur during the charging/discharging process, and Na<sup>+</sup> can diffuse faster. Thus, it indicates Co doping is more favorable to the diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup> within NCCMT material.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0047_R_d37607434e934" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Batteries Supercaps">47</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="apj3116-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/e73825ba-a856-4ec4-be5b-ee4533277db5/apj3116-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/e73825ba-a856-4ec4-be5b-ee4533277db5/apj3116-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/1841c366-151e-4e32-a63c-59ea18ce0c69/apj3116-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/e73825ba-a856-4ec4-be5b-ee4533277db5/apj3116-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">FIGURE 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=apj3116-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fapj.3116" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">(a) Migration energy barriers for NCCMT and NCMT. (b) NCMT initial structural diagram. (c) Structure of NCCMT after Co-doping. (d) Na<sup>+</sup> diffusivity and GITT curves as a function of voltage for the NCCMT cathode material in the first two cycles. (e) NCCMT CV curves of NCCMT cathode at various scan rates. (f) Fitted linear curves for different scan rates versus peak current in CV measurements.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>To investigate the diffusion kinetics of Na<sup>+</sup> in NCCMT material, we carried out cyclic voltammetry (CV) measurement and galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT). As demonstrated by Figure&nbsp;<a href="#apj3116-fig-0004">4d</a>, the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient of NCCMT material during the first two cycles shows high Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics between 1.21窶嘉冷10<sup>竏9</sup> and 6.37窶嘉冷10<sup>竏10</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>竏1</sup>. The results not only confirm the excellent Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics of the material but also indicate the sodium ion diffusion reversibility.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0048_R_d37607434e982" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Electrochem Commun">48</a>-<a href="#apj3116-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0050_R_d37607434e982" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Bull Mater Sci">50</a></sup></span> Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a> shows the GITT of NCCMT material in the voltage range of 2窶4.3&nbsp;V. The reasons for the excellent rate performance of NCCMT cathode materials in SIBs were investigated by CV measurements. The NCCMT cathode CV curves for different scan rates, which range from 10 to 44窶盈V窶鋭<sup>竏1</sup>, are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#apj3116-fig-0004">4e</a>. The oxidation peak is about 3.15窶鰻 and the reduction peak is about 2.42窶鰻 representing de-sodiation/sodiation progress in the lattice structure. The oxidation and reduction peaks, which are displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#apj3116-fig-0004">4f</a>, progressively shift to higher and lower potentials, respectively, as the scan rate increases. The b values of Peak1 and Peak2 are 0.73 and 0.68 calculated from the linear fit, respectively. Capacitive storage and the diffusion process together control the storage behavior of the NCCMT cathode, according to the calculated results. As the increasing of scan rate, the proportion of capacitive contribution increases.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0051_R_d37607434e997" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - ACS Nano">51</a>, <a href="#apj3116-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0052_R_d37607434e997" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - J Phys Chem C">52</a></sup></span> As seen in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a>, NCCMT material CV curves were tested at a scanning rate of 0.1&nbsp;mV窶鋭<sup>竏1</sup> within 2窶4&nbsp;V and 2窶4.3&nbsp;V in order to learn more about the material electrochemical reaction mechanism. The CV curves within 2窶4&nbsp;V basically overlap during the first two cycles, indicating that the electrochemical reaction in the material has good reversibility. In the CV curves of Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a> a.b, the obvious reversible redox peaks are 2.69窶鰻/2.91窶鰻 and 2.71窶鰻/2.95窶鰻, with a slight shift of the peaks, exhibiting the complex transition of phases that occurs between charging and discharging. These different degrees of phase transitions correspond to the long and short platforms of the charge and discharge curves. Moreover, the phase transition is also due to the slip of the transition metal layer (MO<sub>2</sub>), which makes the sodium ion coordination polyhedron in the O phase and P phase conversion or the change of Na<sup>+</sup> vacancies.<span><sup><a href="#apj3116-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="apj3116-bib-0053_R_d37607434e1013" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - Energ Environ Sci">53</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <p>To further evaluate the electrochemical performance of NCCMT cathode material, full-cell system was applied with hard carbon (HC) as the anode in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#apj3116-fig-0005">5</a>. A voltage range of 1.8窶4.1&nbsp;V was used to test the full-cell electrochemical performance in order to analyze its commercial utility. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#apj3116-fig-0005">5a</a> illustrates that at 0.1 C the full cell first cycle discharge specific capacity was 112.8 mAh g<sup>竏1</sup>. The first cycle reversible specific capacity of the HC anode was 492 mAh g<sup>竏1</sup> in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#apj3116-fig-0005">5b</a>. The capacity retention rate was still 82.17% after 100窶営ycles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#apj3116-fig-0005">5c</a>). And the charge窶電ischarge curves overlapped well, implying that the de-sodiation of sodium ions in the full-cell system also has good reversibility. At 1 C current density, there is still a high discharge specific capacity of 109.9 mAh g<sup>竏1</sup> in the first cycle, and the capacity retention rate is 80.5% after 400窶営ycles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#apj3116-fig-0005">5d</a>). The full-cell reversible specific capacity is nearly comparable to the half-cell, indicating that sodium ions can migrate well to the positive side during charging and discharging. The full battery of this material shows excellent rate and long cycle performance and has good potential application prospects.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="apj3116-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/3765384d-34b1-44e0-bbe8-8dc75f8ae1e4/apj3116-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/3765384d-34b1-44e0-bbe8-8dc75f8ae1e4/apj3116-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/36b338b1-e949-447c-8eba-56f63261e73a/apj3116-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/3765384d-34b1-44e0-bbe8-8dc75f8ae1e4/apj3116-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">FIGURE 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=apj3116-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fapj.3116" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical properties of NCCMT//HC full cell system. (a) Initial three cycles of the charge窶電ischarge curve at 1 C of NCCMT//HC full cell. (b) The hard carbon anode and NCCMT cathode charge窶電ischarge curves, respectively. Cycling performance of the full-cell at 0.1 C (c) and 1 C (d).</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="apj3116-sec-0007">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="apj3116-sec-0007-title">4 CONCLUSION</h2>
         
         <p>In this paper, a newly high-entropy O3-NaNi<sub>0.3</sub> Co<sub>0.2</sub> Cu<sub>0.1</sub> Mn<sub>0.2</sub> Ti<sub>0.2</sub> O<sub>2</sub> cathode material for sodium-ion batteries has been successfully synthesized. The high-entropy NCCMT consists of five elements, providing the material with outstanding structural stability, the coordination of multiple components can significantly improve the cyclic performance of the material at high rates. It provides a reversible capacity of nearly 132 mAh g<sup>竏1</sup> at 0.2 C with long-term cycling stability (81.92% capacity retention after 200窶営ycles) and excellent rate performance (84.90% capacity retention after 1,500窶営ycles at a current density of 80 C). CV and GITT measurements showed that NCCMT reveals a high diffusion rate of Na<sup>+</sup>. And the synthesized NCCMT has a superior compatibility with the HC anode, providing a reversible capacity of 112.8 mAh g<sup>竏1</sup> at a current density of 0.1 C (energy density of ~361.19窶姥h窶洩g<sup>竏1</sup>). High-entropy configuration strategy can effectively suppress complex phase transitions, then further improve structural stability and achieve superior long-cycle stability. Our research indicates that developing high-entropy configurations is a useful approach for creating cathode materials with superior performance for SIBs.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="apj3116-sec-0008">

         </section>
